Row[2] = New onset, symptomatic atrial fibrillation/flutter.  The patient is a pleasant 68-year-old female who presents on this admission with recent difficulty with intermittent palpitations and found to have new onset atrial fibrillation/flutter with controlled ventricular response.  She is currently rate controlled and symptomatically much improved.  She has not converted overnight despite IV Cardizem.  She was also placed on IV heparin.  She describes a history of factor 5 Leiden deficiency, but has not been historically systemically anticoagulated since a prior deep venous thrombosis at age 22.  She apparently was seen and evaluated by the Zangmeister Center and it was not felt necessary at that time that she remained on anticoagulation and she has done well in the interim.  She reports a recent upper respiratory tract infection that seemed to exacerbate her palpitations and now identification of new onset atrial fibrillation/flutter.  I reviewed the details of this diagnosis with her and her husband in detail.  I have advised she undergo transesophageal echocardiography-guided cardioversion and will attempt to perform this later today.  We will await the results of her transesophageal echocardiography prior to making further recommendations regarding rate control versus rhythm control medications.  Her CHA2DS2-VASc score will require chronic systemic anticoagulation going forward.  She will also need a screening followup noninvasive cardiac stress test giving multiple cardiac risk factors as well as reassessment of her sleep apnea.  We will await the results of her TEE-guided cardioversion prior to making additional recommendations.  Other detailed medical problems as highlighted above.
